Refutation of One Act Under Two Powers
Nasafi refutes the argument that one act cannot be under two powers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's refutation of the claim that a single act can be under both God's and the servant's power, and why this leads to theological absurdity.

Core Idea
One act under two powers leads to shirk or impossibility.

This passage presents Imam Nasafi's decisive refutation of a key Mu'tazili argument. He first exposes the logical trilemma about blame, then demolishes the analogy from the witnessed world, and finally demonstrates that the claim inevitably leads to associating partners with God or to logical contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the trilemma
Understand the three options for blame and why only one is coherent. This sets up the problem of dual agency.
Notice the poetic form of the trilemma.
2
Examine the opponents' argument
They analogize from the witnessed world, claiming the unseen must follow the same rules of possibility.
3
Follow Nasafi's refutation
He shows the analogy fails because it leads to absurdities like combining opposites, which violates reason and intuition.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the consequences
The claim leads to shirk (partners with God), jabr (compulsion), or ta'jiz (incapacitation of God) – all impossible.
These are the three logical outcomes; each is unacceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا تعدو أفعالنا التي نذم بها إحدى ثلاث خلال حين نحصيها إما تفرد مولانا بصنعته فيسقط اللوم عنا حين نأتيها أو كان يشركنا فاللوم يلحقه إن كان يلحقنا من لاتم فيها أو لم يكن للإله في خليقته صنع فما الذنب إلا ذنب جانيها
قالوا: وكذا دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين في الشاهد، ولا يختلف الشاهد والغائب في الجائز والممتنع كما في الجمع بين السواد والبياض، فصار مدعي إمكان دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين في الغائب كونه ممتنعا في الشاهد كمدعي إمكان الجمع بين السواد والبياض والحركة والسكون في الغائب، مع كون ذلك مستحيلاً في الشاهد، وهذا خروج عن قضية المعقول، وإبطال الدلائل ونقض البداهة.
وكذا القول به يؤدي إلى جعل العباد شركاء الله تعالى في تحصيل الأفعال، لأنها تحصل بقدرته تعالى وبقدرتهم، والقول بإثبات الشريك الله تعالى في تخليق العالم كفر صراح، وخروج عن التوحيد إلى القول بالتثنية، وكذا القول به يؤدي إلى أن يكون العباد مضطرين في أفعالهم أو يؤدي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى، وكلا الأمرين بين الإحالة ظاهر الفساد، وما أدى إلى ما هو المحال كان محالاً ممتنعا في نفسه.
Our actions that we blame do not exceed three kinds when we enumerate them: either our Master is unique in His making, so blame falls from us when we do them; or He shares with us, so blame attaches to Him if blame attaches to us from the one who has no share in them; or there is no making by God in His creation, so the sin is only the sin of the one who commits it. They said: Likewise, the inclusion of a single object of power under the power of two powerful agents in the witnessed world – and the witnessed and the unseen do not differ in the possible and the impossible, just as with the combination of blackness and whiteness – so the one who claims the possibility of a single object of power under the power of two powerful agents in the unseen, given that it is impossible in the witnessed world, becomes like the one who claims the possibility of combining blackness and whiteness, or motion and rest, in the unseen, despite such being impossible in the witnessed world. This is a departure from the dictate of reason, an invalidation of proofs, and a violation of intuition. Likewise, holding this view leads to making servants partners of God Almighty in producing actions, because they are produced by His power and by their power. And the statement confirming a partner to God Almighty in creating the world is outright disbelief, a departure from monotheism to dualism. Also, holding this view leads either to servants being compelled in their actions or to rendering God Almighty incapable – both matters are obviously absurd and manifestly corrupt, and whatever leads to what is absurd is itself absurd and impossible in itself.
Source pages p. 856

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that a single act cannot fall under two powers simultaneously. It begins with a poetic couplet presenting a trilemma: if God alone creates acts, blame is removed from us; if He shares in them, blame attaches to Him; if He has no part, then sin is solely the sinner's. The opponents then argue by analogy with the witnessed world: in this world, one act cannot be under two agents, and the unseen realm follows the same rules of possibility and impossibility. To claim otherwise is as absurd as claiming blackness and whiteness can coexist. Nasafi then points out that accepting the possibility of one act under two powers leads to shirk (associating partners with God) because it gives servants a share in producing actions alongside God, which is outright disbelief. Alternatively, it entails jabr (compulsion) if God's power overrides, or ta'jiz (incapacitation) of God if the servant's will prevails. Both conclusions are impossible, so the premise is false.

Key Terms
مقدور
قدرة
شاهد
غائب
شرك
توحيد
اضطرار
تعجيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God and the servant can cooperate in creating an act without contradiction.
Correction: Nasafi shows this leads either to shirk (if both contribute) or to jabr/ta'jiz, which are impossible.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi argue is a consequence of claiming that one act is under the power of both God and the servant?
A) It proves human free will.
B) It leads to making servants partners with God in creation, which is disbelief.
C) It is the position of the Jabriyya.
D) It is acceptable in the unseen but not in the witnessed world.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that the claim of one act under two powers leads to either shirk or logical absurdity, thus refuting the Mu'tazili position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever subtly feel that Allah is partly to blame because He created the act and gave you the ability? The trilemma shows that either blame falls entirely on us or on Him—there is no middle ground. How does this shatter any excuse you might make for your sins? Will you now take full responsibility, knowing that your sin is entirely your own choice, while simultaneously acknowledging that Allah creates it?
?
The passage warns that claiming one act under two powers leads either to shirk (making yourself a partner with God) or to jabr (feeling compelled, thus excusing your sin). Which of these two dangers do you lean toward in your heart? Do you ever act as if your desires or circumstances force you to sin? How does the principle that the witnessed and unseen share the same logical rules compel you to reject both extremes and embrace true accountability?
?
If you truly internalize that every action is created by Allah alone—including your obedience and disobedience—how would that change your attitude in worship and repentance? Would you become more humble, knowing you are not the ultimate agent, or more hopeful, knowing Allah is the sole creator of all good? Answer honestly: does this truth make you want to praise Him more or to question His justice? Let the lesson's reasoning settle your heart.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate

The Dilemma of Divine Will and Human Power
Nasafi presents the initial logical fork of divine will and human capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that arises when considering God's will to create an act and the servant's power to refrain from it.

Core Idea
If God wills an act, either the servant can resist or not—both lead to impossibility.

Nasafi begins by setting up a crucial dilemma: when God wills to bring about a servant's act, either the servant has the power to refrain or not. This simple fork already exposes the flaws in both Jabri and Mu'tazili positions. Let us follow his reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two scenarios Nasafi presents.
The first scenario is 'pure compulsion' and the second leads to 'incapacitating God.'
2
Identify the dilemma
See how Nasafi argues that if the servant lacks power to refrain, the act is compelled and that view is corrupt. If the servant has power to refrain, the act may not occur, implying God's will is thwarted.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why this dilemma is important for refuting both Jabriyya and Mu'tazila. The Jabriyya claim compulsion, the Mu'tazila claim full independence.
Nasafi shows both extremes fail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان هذا: أن الله تعالى إذا أراد إيجاد فعل العبد لا يخلو الأمر إما أن كان للعبد قدرة الامتناع أو لم يكن، فإن لم يكن فهو الاضطرار المحض والجبر الصريح إذ الفعل الضروري ما يتولى الله تعالى تخليقه وليس للعبد قدرة دفعه عن نفسه والامتناع عنه كالألوان والهيئات وحركات العروق النابضة وأشباه ذلك، والقول به فاسد يعرف فساده بالضرورة والعقل على ما مر في إبطال كلام الجبرية، وإن كان للعبد قدرة الامتناع فلا يحصل هذا الفعل، فلا يثبت ما هو مقدور الله تعالى إذا اختار العبد الامتناع عنه، فيؤدي إلى تعجيز الله جل الله عن ذلك وذلك باطل، وكذا لو أراد العبد تحصيله إن لم تكن الله تعالى قدرة الامتناع عنه فهو مضطر فيما يفعل؛ لأن فعل ما لا قدرة للفاعل على الامتناع عنه وتحصيل ضده فعل ضروري والقول به كفر، وإن كان الله تعالى قدرة الامتناع وكان العبد مضطرًا إذ ليس له قدرة استجلابه عند قصده إلى ذلك إذا امتنع الله تعالى، ولا قدرة دفعه إذا أوجده الله تعالى. وهذا هو حد الفعل الاضطراري، ولأن من أفعال العباد ما هو قبيح وسفه وإيجاد القبيح قبيح وإيجاد السفه سفه، وموجد ذلك سفيه لأن الإيجاد فوق المباشرة والاكتساب عندكم، ثم مباشرة القبيح قبيحة ومباشرة السفه سفه فالإيجاد أولى أن يكون كذلك، وكذا الموجد أولى أن يكون سفيها من المباشرة، وكذا يلزمون الظلم والجور على هذا الوجه.
على أن ادعاء معنى وراء الوجود تصير به الذات فاعلاً ادعاء أمر غير معقول، فكان مدعي ذلك خارجًا عن قضية العقول. وهذه هي الشبه المعروفة لهم اقتصرنا عليه وأعرضنا عما سواها مخافة التطويل.
The explanation of this: when God Almighty wills to bring about the servant's act, the matter is either that the servant has the power to refrain or not. If he does not have it, then it is pure compulsion and outright coercion, for the necessary act is what God Almighty creates and the servant has no power to repel or refrain from it, like colors, shapes, pulsating vein movements, and the like. Holding this view is corrupt, its corruption known by necessity and reason, as previously mentioned in refuting the speech of the Jabriyya. If the servant has the power to refrain, then this act does not occur, so what is within God's power is not established if the servant chooses to refrain from it, which leads to incapacitating God – exalted is God above that – and that is false. Also, if the servant wants to bring it about and God does not have the power to refrain from it, then he is compelled in what he does, because doing something that the agent has no power to refrain from or to produce its opposite is a necessary act, and holding that view is disbelief. And if God has the power to refrain and the servant is compelled, because he has no power to bring it about when he intends it if God refrains, and no power to repel it if God brings it into existence. This is the definition of the compelled act. Also, because some of the servant's acts are ugly and foolish, and producing the ugly is ugly and producing the foolish is foolish, and the one who produces it is foolish, because producing is above direct commission and acquisition according to you. Then, directly committing the ugly is ugly and committing the foolish is foolish, so producing is even more so. Likewise, the producer is more deserving of being called foolish than the direct committer. Similarly, they attribute injustice and tyranny in this manner. Moreover, claiming a meaning beyond existence by which the essence becomes an agent is a claim of something unintelligible, so the claimant of that departs from the dictate of intellects. These are their well-known doubts; we have confined ourselves to them and turned away from others for fear of lengthening.
Source pages p. 857

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed refutation of both the Mu'tazila and the Jabriyya concerning the interplay of divine and human power. Nasafi sets up a dilemma: when God wills an act, either the servant has the power to refrain or not. If not, the act is compelled, like involuntary bodily movements, which is the Jabri position – false by necessity. If the servant does have the power to refrain, then the act may not occur if the servant chooses to resist, which would mean God's will is frustrated (ta'jiz), an impossibility. Conversely, if God forces the act despite the servant's opposition, it becomes coercion, which is equally false. The same reasoning applies if the servant desires an act and God refrains: the servant is then compelled by God's withholding. Nasafi defines the compelled act as one where the agent lacks power to prevent or produce its opposite. He then addresses the objection that attributing evil acts to God would make Him unjust: if the servant directly commits evil, that is evil; but if God produces that evil (by creating the act as the servant acquires it), then God would be even more directly involved and thus more deserving of blame. Finally, he rejects the idea of a 'meaning' beyond existence that would make an essence an agent, calling it unintelligible, and concludes by noting that these are the main doubts of the opponents.

Key Terms
اضطرار
جبر
قدرة الامتناع
تعجيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God wills an act, it must happen regardless of human choice.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if the servant has the power to refrain, the act may not occur, otherwise God would be incapacitated—an impossibility.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what follows if the servant has the power to refrain from an act God wills?
A) The act occurs by God's power alone.
B) The act may not occur, leading to incapacitating God.
C) The servant is compelled to do the act.
D) The act is a case of acquisition (kasb).

Key Takeaway
The initial dilemma shows that neither pure compulsion nor full human independence can be maintained without absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you find yourself attributing it to God's decree to avoid responsibility? How does this dilemma's rejection of pure compulsion confront that tendency?
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if your choices are completely independent of God's will? What would change if you truly internalized that every action you perform is only possible because God wills it?
?
This passage strips away the comfortable extremes of fatalism and absolute free will. Which horn do you naturally lean toward, and what would it cost you to abandon that false comfort for the tension of kasb?

The Definition of the Compelled Act
Nasafi defines the compelled act and states that holding it is disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a compelled act and why it leads to disbelief when attributed to God.

Core Idea
A compelled act is one that the agent cannot prevent or produce an opposite.

After the initial dilemma, Nasafi turns to define the compelled act (al-fi'l al-idtirari). He explores the converse scenario: if the servant desires an act but God refrains, the servant is compelled. This definition is crucial for distinguishing human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the definition of the compelled act.
Note the two conditions: no power to bring about if God refrains, no power to repel if God creates.
2
Understand the definition
Nasafi says a compelled act is when the agent lacks power to bring it about when intending it if God refrains, and lacks power to repel it if God brings it into existence.
This defines pure compulsion from both ends.
3
See the implications
Consider why holding that God compels acts leads to kufr: it makes God responsible for evil and negates human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان هذا: أن الله تعالى إذا أراد إيجاد فعل العبد لا يخلو الأمر إما أن كان للعبد قدرة الامتناع أو لم يكن، فإن لم يكن فهو الاضطرار المحض والجبر الصريح إذ الفعل الضروري ما يتولى الله تعالى تخليقه وليس للعبد قدرة دفعه عن نفسه والامتناع عنه كالألوان والهيئات وحركات العروق النابضة وأشباه ذلك، والقول به فاسد يعرف فساده بالضرورة والعقل على ما مر في إبطال كلام الجبرية، وإن كان للعبد قدرة الامتناع فلا يحصل هذا الفعل، فلا يثبت ما هو مقدور الله تعالى إذا اختار العبد الامتناع عنه، فيؤدي إلى تعجيز الله جل الله عن ذلك وذلك باطل، وكذا لو أراد العبد تحصيله إن لم تكن الله تعالى قدرة الامتناع عنه فهو مضطر فيما يفعل؛ لأن فعل ما لا قدرة للفاعل على الامتناع عنه وتحصيل ضده فعل ضروري والقول به كفر، وإن كان الله تعالى قدرة الامتناع وكان العبد مضطرًا إذ ليس له قدرة استجلابه عند قصده إلى ذلك إذا امتنع الله تعالى، ولا قدرة دفعه إذا أوجده الله تعالى. وهذا هو حد الفعل الاضطراري، ولأن من أفعال العباد ما هو قبيح وسفه وإيجاد القبيح قبيح وإيجاد السفه سفه، وموجد ذلك سفيه لأن الإيجاد فوق المباشرة والاكتساب عندكم، ثم مباشرة القبيح قبيحة ومباشرة السفه سفه فالإيجاد أولى أن يكون كذلك، وكذا الموجد أولى أن يكون سفيها من المباشرة، وكذا يلزمون الظلم والجور على هذا الوجه.

The explanation of this: when God Almighty wills to bring about the servant's act, the matter is either that the servant has the power to refrain or not. If he does not have it, then it is pure compulsion and outright coercion, for the necessary act is what God Almighty creates and the servant has no power to repel or refrain from it, like colors, shapes, pulsating vein movements, and the like. If the servant has the power to refrain, then this act does not occur, so what is within God's power is not established if the servant chooses to refrain from it, which leads to incapacitating God – exalted is God above that – and that is false. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates all acts, humans are not morally responsible.
Correction: Nasafi shows that true compulsion (where the agent cannot prevent or produce) makes the act necessary and holding that view is disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the definition of a compelled act?
A) An act that God creates without human involvement.
B) An act that the agent has no power to bring about or prevent.
C) An act that is evil and deserving of blame.
D) An act that God wills but the servant does not.

Key Takeaway
The compelled act is one where the agent has no power to bring about or prevent it; holding that all acts are compelled is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused a sin by telling yourself that God created this action in you? How does Nasafi's definition of the compelled act challenge that excuse and call you to take full ownership of your choices?
?
If you truly believed that every one of your actions is compelled by God, would you feel any genuine accountability to Him for your deeds? What does this lesson reveal about the hidden danger of that belief in your own heart?
?
When you find yourself powerless to do a good deed or to avoid a sin, do you secretly blame God for not giving you the ability? How does this passage redefine your compulsion and remind you of your responsibility to seek His help?
